Eggeling
  1. The ≈öukra and Manthin grahas he draws first, for thereby the Soma feast comes to be supplied with pure Soma (≈õukra). Thereupon the ƒÄgraya·πáa, for that (cup) is drawn at all (three) feasts. Then the Marutvatƒ´ya cup; then the Ukthya, for here also there are songs of praise (Uktha) 3.

Eggeling
  1. Now some draw the Marutvatƒ´ya after they have drawn the Ukthya; but let him. not do this,–let him rather draw the Ukthya after he has drawn the Marutvatƒ´ya.

‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã- ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•à‡§É ‡•§ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•™ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§è‡§∑‡§É ‘‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à’ ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç’ ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‘‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§É’ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡§É ‡•§ “‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡•á ‡§°‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É” (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß ‡•§ ‡•´‡•Æ ‡§µ‡§æ. ‡•ß ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡•á)- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§°‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§É ‡•§ “‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‚Äù (‡§§‡•à. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•¨ ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•©) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‚Äò‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø’ ‡•§ ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§£‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•• ‡•™ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. These, then, are five grahas he draws; for that midday PavamƒÅna chant is a thunderbolt: hence it is a fifteenfold five-hymned chant 4, for the thunderbolt is fifteenfold 5. He is so by means of these five grahas (cups of Soma 6): for five are these fingers, and with the fingers he hurls (the thunderbolt).

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ω‡§®‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§µ‡§§‡•á- ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ω‡§®‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡•ã S‡§è‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§è‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•´ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡•ã ‡§è‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ’ ‘‡§è‡§∑‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‘‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§É’ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•à‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•à‡§É ‘‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•á’ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‘‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‘‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ’ ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡•á’ ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‘‡§Ö‡§≠‡§Ø‡•á’ ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•á’ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á ‘‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø’ ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§™‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§ò‡§æ‡§§‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•´ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Indra hurled the thunderbolt at VrÃ•tra; and having smitten VrÃ•tra, the wicked, and safety and peace being secured 7, he led forth the dakshi·πáƒÅs (gifts to priests). Wherefore now also, when they (the UdgƒÅtrÃ•s) chant the midday PavamƒÅna, and safety and peace are secured, the dakshi·πáƒÅs are led forth. And so, forsooth, does he now by means of those five cups of Soma hurl the thunderbolt at the wicked, hateful enemy, and having smitten VrÃ•tra, the wicked, and safety and peace being

secured, he leads forth the dakshi·πáƒÅs. This is why he draws those five cups.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø- ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§§‡•å ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•å ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç, ‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§£” ‡•§ (‡§∂. ‡§™. ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•≠-‡•Ø) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‘‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç-‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§

‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§™‡§ø Eggeling
  1. Then as to why he draws the Marutvatƒ´ya cups. Now this, the midday pressing feast, is Indra’s special (nishkevalya) feast: thereby he strove to smite VrÃ•tra, thereby he strove to vanquish him. But the Maruts, having on that account 8 withdrawn, were standing on an A≈õvattha tree 9 (Ficus Religiosa). Now Indra is the nobility, and the Maruts are the people, and through the people the noble becomes strong: therefore the two Ritu cups (they say) 10 may be of a≈õvattha wood; but in reality they are of kƒÅrshmarya wood.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. He said, ‘Do ye join me with vigour!’–‘Then draw a third cup for us;’ they said. He drew a third cup for them, with, ‘Thou art taken with a support,–thee for the vigour of the Maruts!’ They then joined him with vigour,–and he conquered with them, and smote VrÃ•tra with them;–for Indra is the nobility, and the Maruts are the people, and through the people the noble becomes strong. Hence he now bestows that strength on the nobility, and therefore he draws the Marutvatƒ´ya cups.

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç- ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§π ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•¶ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡•á ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ç- ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø- ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‘‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§É’ ‘‡§Ü‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‘‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç’ ‘‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§§‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‘‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø’ ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‘‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á’ ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‘‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡•• ‡•ß‡•¶ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Let him draw them for Indra Marutvat (accompanied by the Maruts), and not for the Maruts likewise. For were he also to draw cups for the Maruts, he would make the people refractory to the nobility. He thus assigns to the Maruts a share therein after Indra, whereby he makes the people subservient and obedient to the nobility: therefore let him draw the cups for Indra Marutvat, and not for the Maruts likewise.

‡•ß‡•ß

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™) ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§π‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡••
‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™) ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§π‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡••
‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§π‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡••
‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡•ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞ ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•ß ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§¢‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§è‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã’ ‘‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞’ ‡•§ “‡§≠‡•Ä‡§π‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§≠‡•É‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•Å‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö” (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•ß ‡•§ ‡•©‡•Ø) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‘‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‘‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‘‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É’ ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‘‡§® ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø; ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‘‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‘‡§Ö‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§’ ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç, ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ’ ‘‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‘‡§®’ ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ç ‘‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡•• ‡•ß‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. But he was afraid of their desertion,–‘Lest they should desert me, lest they should take to some other (party) 12,’ so thinking, he by that (share in the libation) made them unwilling to desert him. This is why he should draw the grahas for Indra Marutvat.

‡•ß‡•®

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§Ω) ‡§ã‡§§‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••
(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É) ‡§ã‡§§·≥ò‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§¶‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡§µ‡§®‡•á·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•É‡§§‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•á ‡§∏·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•á·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§µ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•É‡§§‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø[[!!]] ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∂‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∂ ‡§Ω‡§ã‡§§·≥ò‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§á‡§¶·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§§‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§Ω) ‡§ã‡§§‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

Eggeling
  1. He draws them with the two vessels of the seasons, for the year, the sacrifice, means the seasons. There, at the morning Soma feast, they are overtly attended to, in that he draws the grahas for the seasons 14; and now they are covertly attended

to, in that he draws the Marutvatƒ´ya grahas with the two vessels of the seasons.

‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§£ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É- ‡§π‡•á ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É’ ! ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•å “‡§Æ‡§§‡•Å‡§µ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§∞‡•Å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•å ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡§ø” (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•Æ ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•ß) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§á‡§π’ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‘‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§Ç’ ‘‡§™‡§æ‡§π‡§ø’ ‡§™‡§ø‡§¨ ‡•§ “‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡§ø” (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•® ‡•§ ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•≠‡•¨) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§™‡•ã ‡§≤‡•Å‡§ï‡§ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§¨‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡§ø‡§¨‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø- ‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§É, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§É, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‘‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ’ ‘‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø’ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø‡§¨‡§É’ ‡§™‡•Ä‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡•á ‡§∂‡•Ç‡§∞ ! ‘‡§§‡§µ’ ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡•Ä’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ, ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•à‡§ï‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§à‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‘‡§∏‡•Å‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§É’ ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§É ‘‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‘‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‘‡§§‡§µ’ ‘‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç (‡§®‡§ø‡§ò‡§Ç‡•¶ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•¶) ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π ! ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ñ‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‘‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§É’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‘‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á’ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•© ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He draws (the first) from that (stream of Soma) 15, with (VƒÅj. S. VII, 35; Rig-veda III, 51, 7), ‘O Indra, leader of the Maruts, drink thou the Soma here, as thou drankest of the liquor at (the sacrifice of) the Son of SaryƒÅti: by thy guidance, in thy protection, O Lord, do the wise serve thee with good offerings!–Thou art taken with a support: thee to Indra Marutvat!–This is thy womb: thee to Indra Marutvat!’

“‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ï‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡•Ç‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡•á‡§Æ ‡•§ ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á, ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•å‡§ú‡§∏‡•á”- (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•≠ ‡•§ ‡•©‡•´) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•ß‡•™ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É- ‘‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç’ 16 ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‚Äò‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‘‡§Ö‡§ï‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É, ‘‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç, ‘‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§∏‡§π‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‘‡§â‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§∏‡§π‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§¨‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§É ‘‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§®‡•Ç‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‡§®‡§µ‡•Ä‡§®‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‘‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡•á’ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‘‡§á‡§π’ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á, ‘‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡•á‡§Æ’ ‡§Ü‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§

‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç 17 ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π ! ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‘‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø’ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ú‡§∏‡•á ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•™ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. [The second he draws 18 with VƒÅj. S. VII, 36;

Rig-veda III, 47, 5], ‘The mighty bull, followed by the Maruts, the bountiful, divine ruler Indra,–him, the all-subduing, the terrible bestower of victory, do we now invoke for new favour.–Thou art taken with a support: thee to Indra Marutvat!–This is thy womb: thee to Indra Marutvat!’–with Thou art

taken with a support: thee for the strength of the Maruts!’ he draws the third cup.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he draws the MƒÅhendra cup. For Indra was then bound up with evil, in the shape of the people, the Maruts; as one might, for the sake of victory, eat from the same vessel with the people 19 so it was when they drew a cup for him in common with the Maruts.

‡•ß‡•¨

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. When all was conquered and free from danger and injury, the gods plucked him from out of all evil–even as one might pluck out a reed from its sheath–when they drew the cup for the Great Indra. And even as the reed becomes leafless, so is he thereby freed from all evil, when one draws the MƒÅhendra cup.

‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É’ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‘‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§É’ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É’ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‘‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç’ ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡•á‡§® ‘‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø’ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‘‡§è‡§µ’ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•≠ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. And again, why he draws the MƒÅhendra cup. Before the slaughter of VrÃ•tra, he was indeed Indra; but when he had slain VrÃ•tra, he became the Great–Indra, even as one who has conquered all around, becomes a Great King (mahƒÅrƒÅja): therefore he draws the MƒÅhendra cup. And, moreover, he forsooth make’s him great for the slaughter of VrÃ•tra therefore also he draws the MƒÅhendra cup. He draws it in the ≈öukra vessel, for bright (≈õukra) and great indeed is he (the sun) that burns yonder: therefore he draws it in the ≈öukra vessel.

Eggeling
  1. He thus draws it from that (Dro·πáakala≈õa or P≈´tabhrÃ•t), with (VƒÅj. S. VII, 39; Rig-veda VI, 19, 1), ‘Great is Indra and hero-like, gladdening the people, of double stature and unimpaired in power. For our sake he waxed strong for heroic deed,–great and broad was he, and

well-shapen by the shapers 21.–Thou art taken with a support: thee to Mahendra!’–with ‘This is thy womb: thee to Mahendra!’ he deposits it; for it is indeed for the Great Indra that he draws it.

Eggeling
  1. And having bespoken (the chant 23), he says this speech,–‘Pressers, press ye! make the mortars

resound! Agnƒ´dh, stir the sour milk! be thou mindful of Soma’s (pap)!’ It is for the evening’s press-feast that those pressers press out (the Soma juice), for the evening feast they make the mortars resound, for the evening feast the Agnƒ´dh stirs the sour milk, for the evening feast he boils the pap for Soma. For these two press-feasts, the morning feast and the midday feast, are indeed rich in pure Soma, are rich in juice; but that third press-feast is emptied of the pure Soma. Hence he forms it from out of this midday feast; and thus that third press-feast becomes for him rich in pure Soma, rich in juice: this is why he now speaks that speech.

  1. 331:2 ‘Iha’ (here, hither) with the last syllable protracted. The HotrÃ•’s cup with the NigrƒÅbhyƒÅ (vasatƒ´varƒ´) water having been handed to the sacrificer, and the fillet or band (ush·πáƒ´sha) with which the Soma-plants are tied together, to the GrƒÅvastut, the pressing is performed in the same way as the ‘great pressing,’ at the PrƒÅta·∏•savana (see p. 256, note 1). Meanwhile the GrƒÅvastut takes the band, and winds it thrice round his head and face from left to right. And whenever Soma-stalks are taken out for pressing he extols the stones by chanting the GrƒÅva-stotra or ‘praise of the stones.’ According to ƒÄ≈õv. ≈ör. V, 12; Ait. Br. VI, 7, 2, this chant consists of the verses Rig-veda I, 24, 3; V, 81, 1; VIII, 81, 1; VIII, 1, 1, followed by the hymn X, 94, ascribed to the serpent RÃ•shi Arbuda. Before the last verse of this hymn he inserts the hymns X, 76 and X, 175, (ascribed to the serpents Jaratkar·πáa and Arbuda respectively); and either before, or between, or after these two hymns he throws in the pƒÅvamƒÅnƒ´·∏• (Rig-veda IX) according to requirement, till the pressing is completed, or the libations are to be drawn, when having wound up with the last verse of the first Arbuda hymn, he makes over the band to the sacrificer. The five cups mentioned in paragraph 2 are filled from the stream of Soma flowing from the HotrÃ•’s cup into the Dro·πáakala≈õa; the ƒÄgraya·πáa (p. 294, note 2) however being taken (in the ƒÄgraya·πáa sthƒÅlƒ´ or bowl) from that and two other streams, poured by the UnnetrÃ• from the ƒÄdhavanƒ´ya, and by the PratiprasthƒÅtrÃ• from some vessel containing the Soma previously kept in the ƒÄgraya·πáa sthƒÅlƒ´. ↩︎

These are chanted in such a way as to produce five SƒÅman hymns (i.e. a hymn of three verses), viz. the gƒÅyatrƒ´ triplet is chanted twice, in the GƒÅyatra and ƒÄmahƒ´yava tunes;–the brÃ•hatƒ´-satobrÃ•hatƒ´ couplet is likewise chanted twice, in the Raurava and YaudhƒÅjaya tunes, the two verses being as usual (by the repetition of certain pƒÅdas) made into three. These, with the addition of the trish·π≠ubh hymn, chanted in the Au≈õana tune, make five SƒÅman hymns of three verses each, or altogether fifteen verses (pa√±cada≈õastoma). ↩︎

  18. 336:2 Here the author again anticipates, important parts of the performance being not even referred to. On the present occasion only one Marutvatƒ´ya cup is drawn and deposited on the mound (khara). The Ukthya cup having then been drawn and deposited, the priests leave the HavirdhƒÅna in the same way as at the morning performance (see IV, 2, 5, 1, with note), and perform the Vipru·∏ç-homas, or drop-offerings. Thereupon the priests ‘creep’ (sarp), with their upper bodies bent parallel to the ground, to the Sadas, where, near the Udumbara post, the chanting of the midday PavamƒÅna-stotra now takes place after the necessary preliminaries. If the Pravargya has been performed on the preceding day (see III, 4, 4, 1, with note), the Dadhi-gharma, or libation of hot milk mixed with sour milk, is now made. Then follow the oblations from the Savanƒ´ya-puro·∏çƒÅ≈õa (see IV, 2, 5, 15 seq., and p. 323, note ). Thereupon filling of the cups of the ten Camasins, and the libations from (and drinking of) the ≈öukra and Manthin cups. After the eating of the I·∏çƒÅ of the puro·∏çƒÅ≈õas, the DƒÅkshi·πáa-homas and distribution of the sacrificial fees take place, as set forth in the next BrƒÅhma·πáa. Thereupon the Adhvaryu calls on the MaitrƒÅvaru·πáa to pronounce the invitatory prayer to Indra Marutvat (viz. Rig-veda III, 51, 7), ‘O Indra, attended by the Maruts, here drink the Soma,’ &c., followed by the order (praisha), ‘Let the HotrÃ• pronounce the offering prayer to Indra Marutvat!’ The PratiprasthƒÅtrÃ• now draws a second Marutvatƒ´ya cup in the other Ritu-pƒÅtra. The offering prayer (Rig-veda III, 47, 2, ‘United with the host of Maruts, O Indra, drink the Soma, O wise hero!’ &c.) having meanwhile been pronounced by the HotrÃ•, the Adhvaryu makes libations from the first cup at the Vasha·π≠ and Anuvasha·π≠. Then pouring the remains of the juice into some other vessel, to be taken to the Sadas, he enters the HavirdhƒÅna and draws the third Marutvatƒ´ya graha with the cup just emptied. Having deposited it, he betakes himself to. the Sadas to drink with the HotrÃ• the remains of the first libation. Thereupon the HotrÃ• recites the Marutvatƒ´ya ≈öastra. ↩︎

  23. 339:2 That is, the (first) PrÃ•sh·π≠·∏•a-stotra, consisting of the Rathantara-sƒÅm an, SƒÅmav. II, 30-31. For the way in which the two verses are manipulated (by repetition of the last pƒÅda of the first, and of the second pƒÅda of the second verse), so as to yield a three-versed choral, see Haug, Ait. Br. II, p. 198; Weber, Ind. Stud. VIII, p. 25. These chants derive their name from the circumstance that the SƒÅmans employed in them are capable of being used as ‘prÃ•sh·π≠·∏•as,’ that is, of being chanted twice with another SƒÅman inserted between them,–or, to speak symbolically, to serve as the womb for the reception of an embryo. For this purpose the Rathantara and BrÃ•hat SƒÅmans are chiefly used. See note on IV, 5, 4, 13. Whenever the PrÃ•sh·π≠·∏•as are chanted in this way (which they are not at the ordinary Agnish·π≠oma), it is chiefly at this very place in the Soma performance, at the midday libation. The chant is succeeded by the recitation, by the HotrÃ•, of the Nishkevalya ≈öastra, consisting of the following parts. The ƒÄhƒÅva (and pratigara) is followed by the Stotriya (Rig-veda VII, 32, 22-23, identical with the Rathantara) and Anur≈´pa (VIII, 3, 7-8) pragƒÅthas; then a dhƒÅyyƒÅ, X, 74,.6; the SƒÅma-pragƒÅtha, VIII, 3, 1, and the hymn (to Indra) I, 32, with the Nivid inserted in the middle (after the eighth verse). Finally the HotrÃ• pronounces the Ukthavƒ´rya, and the offering prayer, VII, 22, 1, after which the MƒÅhendra libation is poured into the fire.Then follows the distribution of the Ukthya graha among the three assistants of the HotrÃ• and the recitation of their (nishkevalya) ≈õastras–each preceded by a PrÃ•sh·π≠·∏•a-stotra [SƒÅmav. II, 32-34 (chanted to the VƒÅmadevya-sƒÅman); 35-36 (Naudhasa); 37-38 (KƒÅleya) respectively]–as at the conclusion of the morning performance; see , note 2. Thereupon he addresses the above summons to the respective priests, for the preparations necessary for the evening pressing. ↩︎
